Similarly, the "happiness fluid" narrative treats serotonin as a baseline tonic stabilizer that prevents sadness, a view completely unequipped to explain why 5-HT_2A receptor agonists (like classic psychedelics) produce acute, profound, and often destabilizing reconfigurations of conscious and cognitive structures rather than static contentment.39 The Carhart-Harris bipartite model replaces this with a precise engineering framework: serotonin alternates between a default, high-affinity stress-moderation brake (5-HT_1A for passive coping) and a low-affinity, high-urgency system destabilizer (5-HT_2A for active coping) that opens a transient window of profound structural plasticity to rescue the active inference engine when it becomes trapped in unviable, high-stress loops.39

Finally, the "bad stress chemical" narrative treats cortisol as a biological error that damages health and should be universally suppressed, ignoring that without the morning cortisol awakening response, the organism cannot generate the blood pressure, glucose mobilization, or mental alertness required to initiate interaction with the environment. The chemical tuning-board model frames cortisol as an indispensable resource allocator that scales the systemic ledger to meet anticipated demand.8 Structural damage occurs not from the chemical itself, but from the time-collapse error of chronic, non-resolving activation, which exhausts cellular quality-control buffers and causes Mitochondrial Allostatic Load (MALT), turning an adaptive mobilization tool into a source of systemic biological debt.8

## **20. Reusable Schemas and Tables**

The artifacts compiled in this section represent the exhaustive technical warehouse of the chemical tuning-board model, formatted as clean, structured markdown matrices for direct ingestion by subsequent canon reports.

### **Artifact A: Signal Class Taxonomy**

┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  
│                                         SIGNAL CLASS TAXONOMY                                          │  
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  
│ Classical Neurotransmitters (e.g., Glutamate, GABA)                                                    │  
│  - Signaling Mode: Synaptic Wiring Transmission; direct point-to-point ion channel gating.              │  
│  - Typical Timescale: Milliseconds.                                                                    │  
│  - Spatial Range: Highly localized; restricted strictly to the immediate synaptic cleft.               │  
│  - Examples: Glutamate, GABA, Glycine.                                                                 │  
│  - Primary Regulatory Function: Mediates fast informational transfers; carries raw sensory/motor data. │  
│  - Common Misinterpretation: Framed as isolated switches for thoughts or specific behavioral emotions.  │  
│  - Evidence Caveat: High-speed synaptic measurements require invasive in vitro or animal recordings.    │  
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  
│ Neuromodulators (e.g., Dopamine, Norepinephrine, Acetylcholine, Serotonin)                             │  
│  - Signaling Mode: Volume Transmission; extrasynaptic diffusion via axonal varicosities.       │  
│  - Typical Timescale: Seconds to Minutes.                                                              │  
│  - Spatial Range: Widespread extracellular micro-domains and regional cortical networks.[2, 16]   │  
│  - Examples: Dopamine, Norepinephrine, Acetylcholine, Serotonin.[17, 18]                         │  
│  - Primary Regulatory Function: Adjusts signal-to-noise ratios; tunes precision and action gain.│  
│  - Common Misinterpretation: Mischaracterized as direct causes of raw emotions (e.g., happiness fluid).│  
│  - Evidence Caveat: Extrasynaptic concentration dynamics rely on complex, non-linear clear paths.│  
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  
│ Neuropeptides (e.g., Endogenous Opioids, Oxytocin, Vasopressin)                                        │  
│  - Signaling Mode: High-affinity GPCR activation; vesicular exocytosis from large dense-core vesicles. │  
│  - Typical Timescale: Minutes to Hours.                                                                │  
│  - Spatial Range: Regional and cross-structural volume matrices; lacks localized reuptake paths.        │  
│  - Examples: beta-Endorphin, Enkephalins, Oxytocin, Vasopressin, Orexin/Hypocretin.         │  
│  - Primary Regulatory Function: Functions as macro-scalar state-switchers signaling core safety/crisis.│  
│  - Common Misinterpretation: Labeled as simple mechanical on/off switches for love, pain, or hunger.   │  
│  - Evidence Caveat: Central peptide concentrations dissociate completely from blood serum parameters.  │  
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  
│ Endocrine and Metabolic Hormones (e.g., Cortisol, Insulin, Leptin, Ghrelin, GLP-1)                     │  
│  - Signaling Mode: Systemic Vascular Circulation; active or passive blood-brain barrier transport.     │  
│  - Typical Timescale: Hours to Weeks.                                                                  │  
│  - Spatial Range: Whole-organism coordination; targets central hypothalamic and midbrain hubs.  │  
│  - Examples: Cortisol, Insulin, Leptin, Ghrelin, GLP-1.                          │  
│  - Primary Regulatory Function: Formulates the somatic ledger; updates policy affordability matrices.   │  
│  - Common Misinterpretation: Viewed as independent homeostatic indicators disconnected from cognition. │  
│  - Evidence Caveat: Saturable blood-brain barrier transporter gates create significant transport lag.  │  
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤  
│ Immune Cytokines (e.g., IL-1β, IL-6, TNF-α)                                                            │  
│  - Signaling Mode: Humoral signaling via endothelial claudin-5 disruption and fast vagal lines.│  
│  - Typical Timescale: Days to Months.                                                                  │  
│  - Spatial Range: Systemic-to-central parenchymal re-routing; triggers local microglial activation.    │  
│  - Examples: Interleukin-1 beta, Interleukin-6, Tumor Necrosis Factor-alpha, Interferon-alpha. │  
│  - Primary Regulatory Function: Activates immune-motivational retuning to prioritize healing.  │  
│  - Common Misinterpretation: Interpreted as an accidental psychological failure or defect phenotype.   │  
│  - Evidence Caveat: Peripheral serum inflammation markers show weak spatial correlation centrally.      │  
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

### **Artifact B: Motivational Tuning Matrix**

* **Dopamine:** Tracks reward prediction errors (delta_n) and opportunity costs (R).4 Tonic maintains pacemaker firing; phasic delivers prediction errors.18 Invigorates actions; flattens the effort-discounting curve.5 Updates policy value and reinforces direct-pathway loops.5 Suppressed by high leptin/insulin signals.12 Suppressed by chronic peripheral inflammatory cytokines.14 Optimal range tracks environmental return rates.30 Dysregulation causes habit lock-in, stereotypy, or amotivation. Commonly abused via the "pleasure juice" myth.28 *High confidence*.  
* **Norepinephrine:** Regulates central network gain and arousal under uncertainty.1 Phasic reset vs. elevated tonic global volume diffusion.31 Triggers environmental exploration under model failure.29 Sets baseline vigilance and matches threat survival metrics.31 Stimulates astrocytic glycogenolysis via beta2-AR to fuel active cells.1 Synergizes with cortisol to dismantle prefrontal top-down control.7 Optimal range balances exploit-explore thresholds.29 Dysregulation causes hypervigilance, panic narrowing, or missing cues. Commonly abused via the "panic chemical" trope. *High confidence*.  
* **Acetylcholine:** Tracks expected uncertainty to calculate sensory precision weights.19 Baseline tonic maintenance punctuated by task-locked phasic bursts.16 Boosts bottom-up prediction errors; dampens lateral prior distributions.16 Amplifies sensory attention channels.19 Interacts with NE to balance noise vs. volatility tracking.31 Modulates baseline limbic processing configurations. Optimal range maps environmental cue reliability.32 Dysregulation triggers sensory overload or unyielding stuck priors.19 Commonly abused via the "memory chemical" oversimplification.35 *High confidence*.  
* **Serotonin:** Regulates temporal horizons, behavioral restraint, and stress coping.38 Tonic pacemaker activity; mass surges during critical adversity encounters.38 Suppresses immediate impulsivity; extends waiting patience parameters (gamma).38 Codes aversive prediction errors and punishment probabilities.18 Modulates metabolic satiety gates within hypothalamic hubs.23 Complements cortisol to balance passive tolerance vs. active remodeling.39 Optimal range enforces long-horizon policy calibration.38 Dysregulation causes impulsive choices, learned helplessness, or behavioral rigidity. Commonly abused via the "chemical imbalance" myth.40 *High confidence*.  
* **Endogenous Opioids:** Evaluates hedonic consumption and coordinates relief policies.28 Localized enkephalin/endorphin transients within limbic hotspots.28 Gates sensory "liking" validation; downregulates nociceptive entry lines.28 Restores baseline homeostatic parameters after high exertion.48 Interacts with dopamine to separate wanting from consumptive liking.28 Interacts with oxytocin to reward pair-bond structural continuity.28 Optimal range terminates high-cost motor allocation policies.49 Dysregulation prompts compulsive drug-seeking behavior or complete relief lock-in. Commonly abused via the "runner's high only" myth.48 *High confidence*.  
* **Endocannabinoids:** Controls retrograde homeostatic stabilization and fear extinction learning. Synthesized on-demand via retrograde lipid-derived messengers. Suppresses presynaptic neurotransmitter excitability across glutamate/GABA lines. Attenuates persistent aversive memory precision to signal environmental safety. Downregulates acute HPA-axis hyper-activation following surges. Interacts with opioids to manage physical post-exertion recuperation. Optimal range breaks hypervigilant policy loops to permit flexibility. Dysregulation causes memory consolidation deficits or locked-in paranoia states. Commonly abused via the "intoxicating euphoria switch" trope. *High confidence*.  
* **Oxytocin:** Tunes the sensory precision and salience of interpersonal information.28 Diffuse central volume transmission from paraventricular nodes.9 Amplifies collective trust under safety; sharpens xenophobia under threat.9 Anchors risk distribution and load-sharing bioenergetic calculations.9 Combines with opioids to validate maternal and pair-bond scaffolding.28 Suppresses individual amygdalar HPA driving lines under safety priors.44 Optimal range permits bioenergetic outsourcing to social partners.9 Dysregulation causes pathological dependency or aggressive out-group hostility. Commonly abused via the "love hormone" myth.28 *Moderate confidence*.  
* **Vasopressin:** Dictates social status defense, territorial monitoring, and active protectiveness.44 Co-released systemically and centrally alongside oxytocin vectors.44 Heightens sympathetic autonomic tone; increases threat mobilization vigor.44 Biases the system to interpret ambiguous updates as active boundary threats. Interacts with cortisol to fund immediate physical defense configurations.44 Complements oxytocin to construct the integrated social spatial matrix.9 Optimal range secures territorial assets and group hierarchy structure. Dysregulation drives reactive paranoia, hyper-aggression, or social insulation. Commonly abused via male-essentialist behavioral typing. *Moderate confidence*.  
* **Cortisol:** Directs allostatic resource mobilization and glucose redirection structures.8 Pulsatile circadian rhythm; massive surges during demand errors.8 Restructures the metabolic ledger to optimize central glucose availability.8 Enhances threat-relevant error precision; suppresses long-term paths.31 Triggers gluconeogenesis and lipolysis to fund urgent motor vigor.53 Interacts with cytokines to manage systemic immune-metabolic shunts.8 Optimal range funds high-priority survival actions under demand.8 Dysregulation causes glucocorticoid resistance and mitochondrial fragmentation (MALT).8 Commonly abused via the "toxic stress hormone" label.8 *High confidence*.  
* **Insulin:** Tracks postprandial blood glucose and index-linked metabolic wealth.12 Baseline postprandial secretion; crosses via specialized transcytosis. Enhances striatal dopamine transporter activity to suppress cue salience.13 Dampens hyper-appetitive foraging policies within hypothalamic nodes.12 Interacts with leptin to signal systemic bioenergetic abundance.23 Regulates long-term cortical synaptic plasticity and vascular health. Optimal range coordinates post-consumption energy routing and satiety. Dysregulation drives central insulin resistance, hyperphagia, and decline. Commonly abused via reductionist dietary willpower narratives. *High confidence*.  
* **Leptin:** Signals long-term lipid reserve mass to suppress reward work motivation.12 Continuous secretion proportional to absolute adipose tissue mass.23 Binds VTA LepR to lower progressive ratio breakpoints directly.12 Selectively discounts value of high-effort physical investments.12 Attenuates conditional place preference for substances of abuse.12 Interacts with ghrelin to balance pre- and postprandial motivation.22 Optimal range stabilizes long-term body weight and policy economy.24 Dysregulation drives central leptin resistance, masking available wealth.12 Commonly abused via the simple mechanical "fullness switch" myth. *High confidence*.  
* **Ghrelin:** Signals acute nutritional scarcity to prioritize exploratory foraging vigor.12 Rises sharply during fasting; drops immediately upon gastric entry.22 Binds VTA GHSR to accelerate dopaminergic prediction velocity.12 Elevates progressive ratio breakpoints to fund high-cost acquisition.12 Triggers generalized locomotive arousal and environmental novelty-seeking.12 Counteracts insulin/leptin signaling to reset mesolimbic cost curves.22 Optimal range ensures rapid food asset extraction under deficit.22 Dysregulation drives compulsive hyper-appetitive search or cache lock-in.12 Commonly abused via the reductionist "hunger trigger" label. *High confidence*.  
* **GLP-1:** Manages postprandial satiety and central cellular protection pathways.12 Released by intestinal L-cells and central preproglucagon hindbrain nodes.12 Increases striatal DAT expression to accelerate dopamine clearance.13 Lowers food cravings; dampens cue-driven neural hyperactivity.13 Elevates anti-apoptotic proteins (Bcl-2) to reduce microglial stress.13 Reciprocally balances ghrelin inputs to stabilize glycemic targets.22 Optimal range terminates appetitive search and initiates rest policies.12 Dysregulation causes hyperphagic policy locks and neuroinflammatory load. Commonly abused via "willpower in a syringe" public discourse.13 *High confidence*.  
* **Cytokines:** Directs immune-motivational retuning during somatic bioenergetic crises.15 Baseline tissue monitoring; massive surges during inflammatory insult.26 Suppresses striatal dopamine synthesis and elevates transporter clearance.14 Enforces sickness behavior to shunt resources toward baseline defense.15 Crosses porous blood-brain barrier zones via claudin-5 down-regulation.26 Triggers central PGE2 synthesis to alter temperature and pain parameters.27 Optimal range guarantees absolute funding for critical immune protection.15 Dysregulation causes chronic amotivation, fatigue, and structural atrophy.14 Commonly abused via the "inflammation causes depression" slogan.14 *High confidence*.  
* **Orexin/Hypocretin:** Stabilizes macro-scalar behavioral states and sets arousal thresholds.21

| **Acetylcholine** | Maintains a background precision grid to preserve sensory awareness.16 | Tracks rapid cue reliability updates to gate local plasticity.16 | Triggers receptor desensitization; degrades top-down attention networks. | Isolating basal forebrain volume transmission from local interneuron lines.16 | Confounding active sensory attention gain with passive memory layout storage.35 |

| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Dopamine D1-like vs. D2-like** | Prefrontal working memory stability vs. flexible model updating.5 | Phasic bursts to slow volume transmission bands.6 | Framed as identical components of a singular reward machine. | D1-D2 balance sets the equilibrium between cognitive persistence and policy flexibility.6 | Human PET tracers feature competitive binding limits that miss real-time receptor switching. |
| **Mesolimbic vs. Mesocortical vs. Nigrostriatal DA** | Effort valuation (EVC) vs. goal stabilization vs. motor habit gating.5 | Milliseconds (prediction errors) to hours (tonic costs).4 | Treated as a monolithic indicator of global psychological motivation. | Differentiates striatal motor gating from prefrontal stability and mesolimbic effort calculation.5 | Transgenic structural tracking inputs do not fully match live human connectivity grids. |
| **Serotonin 5-HT1A vs. 5-HT2A vs. 5-HT3** | Limbic stress moderation vs. cortical structural plasticity vs. fast aversive signaling.39 | Seconds to weeks (transcriptional adaptation).39 | Assumes all serotonergic medications operate on a singular mood pathway. | Type 1A mediates baseline stress endurance while Type 2A opens a window of active structural revaluation.39 | Extensive spatial receptor co-localization generates non-linear intracellular cross-talk. |
| **Alpha vs. Beta Adrenergic Signaling** | Prefrontal microcircuit focus vs. astrocytic glycogenolysis and amygdalar hypervigilance.1 | Milliseconds (attention) to hours (metabolic shunts).1 | Postulates that norepinephrine acts as a uniform generator of panic. | Adrenergic receptor affinity branches enforce a non-linear relationship between arousal and cognitive performance.31 | Systemic blocker applications feature poor barrier penetration, confounding peripheral maps. |
| **Muscarinic vs. Nicotinic Acetylcholine** | Pyramidal excitability and prior dampening vs. fast error channel amplification.16 | Milliseconds (nicotinic) to minutes (muscarinic).16 | Reduces acetylcholine to a simple mechanical driver of cognitive memory storage.35 | Nicotinic networks boost bottom-up prediction errors while muscarinic pathways dampen lateral prior lines.34 | Post-mortem tissue assay protocols do not reconstruct the live dynamics of volume transmission.16 |
| **Cannabinoid CB1 vs. CB2 Architecture** | Presynaptic neurotransmitter suppression vs. microglial neuroinflammatory modulation. | Seconds (retrograde feedback) to days (transcription tracking). | Viewed as a singular, uniform switch for driving intoxicating euphoria. | *CB1 coordinates retrograde presynaptic damping while CB2 regulates central neuroimmune responses.* | Exogenous synthetic agonists display extreme variations in efficacy vs. endogenous parameters. |
| **Mu vs. Kappa vs. Delta Opioid Receptors** | Limbic reward "liking" vs. dopamine suppression circuit breakers vs. anxiety dampening.28 | Minutes to hours (enzymatic degradation profiles).20 | Classifies all endogenous opioid peptides as simple mechanical anti-pain blocks.48 | MOR validates consumptive relief while KOR serves as a circuit breaker to halt unviable behavioral investments.28 | Structural receptor heteromerization completely rewrites ligand binding dynamics.47 |
| **Oxytocin vs. Vasopressin Distribution** | Social cue salience tuning vs. territorial status defense and autonomic tone.28 | Minutes (volume matrix diffusion timelines).9 | Presented as separate, gender-essentialist markers of male vs. female behavior. | Oxytocin and vasopressin form an integrated social spatial matrix balancing affiliation against defensive mobilization.9 | Human receptor mapping remains heavily inferred from animal designs due to tracer limits. |
| **Glucocorticoid MR vs. GR Pathways** | Baseline rhythm preservation vs. macro-scalar transcriptional resource redirection.7 | Hours (nuclear translocation) to months (atrophy timelines).8 | Views cortisol as an unmediated driver of immediate neural destruction centrally.8 | The MR-GR ratio determines the transition from baseline circadian tracking to allostatic resource mobilization.8 | Circulating serum measurements do not capture localized tissue resistance parameters.8 |
| **Central vs. Peripheral GLP-1 Pathways** | Striatal DAT expression and cue dampening vs. incretin insulin release and gastric delay.13 | Minutes (vagal reflex) to days (pharmacological stabilization).22 | Defines behavioral alterations purely as a mechanical consequence of slowed stomach motility.22 | Central GLP-1 signaling reconfigures the mesolimbic effort ledger to suppress reward want transients.12 | Therapeutic long-acting formulations cross barrier boundaries in ways distinct from native tracks. |

| **Orexin x Dopamine** | Sustains motivational continuity; prevents policy state fragmentation.21 | Observed Fact / Optogenetic Tasks.50 | **High confidence** | Hypothalamic orexin lines depolarize VTA centers to secure tonic incentive wanting.21 | Limiting orexinergic systems to mechanical feeding triggers in historical models.50 |

### **Artifact G: Motivational State Typology (Expanded Architecture)**

* **High-Vigor Pursuit:** High tonic/phasic dopamine 29, optimal LC transients 31, low cytokines 15, ghrelin.12 Maximizes action invigoration and flattens the effort curve.5 High-yield patch foraging or expansion.30 Risk: compulsive checking and motor stereotypies. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: prevents pathologizing intense task engagement.  
* **Low-Vigor Conservation:** Suppressed dopamine 15, low norepinephrine 31, high cytokines (IL-6, IL-1beta).14 Steepens the effort curve to enforce energy conservation ("can't").15 Sickness conservation during healing or pathogen defense.15 Risk: chronic inflammatory depressive states.14 *High confidence*. Ethical caution: requires clinical tracking rather than moralizing sloth.  
* **Exploratory Curiosity:** High tonic LC norepinephrine 29, high acetylcholine precision 19, prefrontal D2 dominance.5 Lowers goal energy barriers to promote search variance.6 Unexpected uncertainty and patch exhaustion.29 Risk: distractibility and attention deficit profiles.19 *High confidence*. Ethical caution: frames attention shifts as adaptive strategies.  
* **Defensive Mobilization:** GR cortisol surges 7, low-affinity alpha1/beta adrenergic activation 31, vasopressin.44 Restructures glucose economy to fund urgent escape actions.8 Acute threat or boundary violations.8 Risk: panic narrowness and Mitochondrial Allostatic Load (MALT).8 *High confidence*. Ethical caution: recognizes threat realities over somatic weakness assumptions.  
* **Anxious Hypervigilance:** Persistent tonic norepinephrine 31, high baseline cortisol 8, suppressed endocannabinoids, vasopressin.44 Applies continuous hyper-precision to threat validation channels.19 Sustained, unmapped predator matrices. Risk: generalized anxiety states and complete behavioral avoidance. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: prevents treating survival hypervigilance as an unmediated psychological defect.  
* **Appetitive Seeking:** Central gastric ghrelin 12, high mesolimbic dopamine velocity 29, low leptin/insulin.23 Elevates progressive ratio breakpoints to prioritize acquisition.12 Energetic scarcity and nutritional deficit.22 Risk: compulsive binge patterns and addiction policy locks. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: highlights biochemical driving lines over failure-of-will narratives.  
* **Satiety and Inhibition:** Postprandial GLP-1 and insulin 12, high leptin 24, prefrontal D1 dominance.6 Accelerates dopamine clearance via surface DAT to suppress cue salience.13 Post-consumption homeostatic stabilization.22 Risk: metabolic deconditioning and loss of exploratory drive. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: undermines reductionist commercial health moralization models.  
* **Relief-Seeking:** High-urgency aversive prediction errors 18, dynorphin KOR drive 47, sudden mu-opioid activation.28 Prioritizes paths that terminate active somatic or psychological pain.47 Escaping ongoing physical damage or social exclusion. Risk: compulsive drug-seeking and relief policy lock-ins. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: anchors addictive phenotypes to formal pain-relief loops.  
* **Comfort-Seeking:** Endogenous enkephalins in limbic hotspots 28, moderate anandamide endocannabinoid tone. Rewards entry into configurations of low regulatory cost. Post-expenditure recuperation and debt mitigation. Risk: absolute sedentary entrenchment and loss of capacity tracking. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: prevents moralizing the biological necessity of rest.  
* **Social Bonding:** Central oxytocin under safety priors 9, mu-opioid validation 47, low cortisol.9 Downregulates threat vigilance to validate bioenergetic outsourcing.9 Stable risk distribution grids and pair-bonds.9 Risk: pathological social dependencies and out-group hostility. *Moderate confidence*. Ethical caution: avoids romanticizing social signaling systems.  
* **Status Defense:** Central vasopressin (AVP) 44, optimal noradrenergic gain 31, high testosterone. Elevates valuation of dominance and resource control policies.44 Enforces hierarchy boundaries to stabilize group structure under constraint. Risk: reactive aggression and social polarization. *Moderate confidence*. Ethical caution: avoids essentialist framing of hierarchy navigation.  
* **Shame-Linked Withdrawal:** Dynorphin KOR dominance 47, suppressed dopamine 15, high cortisol.8 Terminates active social policies to minimize interpersonal punishment.49 Surviving severe hierarchy rejection or loss of scaffolding. Risk: social phobia and major depressive phenotypes. *Moderate confidence*. Ethical caution: tracks social exclusion as a concrete bioenergetic catastrophe.  
* **Sickness Conservation:** Endothelial activation via prostaglandins (PGE2) 27, IL-6/IL-1beta cytokines 14, claudin-5 loss.26 Shuts down external behavior to fund immune activation.15 Active pathogen invasion and tissue damage.26 Risk: chronic neuroinflammatory fatigue and Long-COVID phenotypes.14 *High confidence*. Ethical caution: critical for legitimizing chronic fatigue syndromes against psychological reductionism.  
* **Sleep Pressure:** Extracellular adenosine accumulation, pineal melatonin saturation, low histaminergic firing.56 Downregulates cortical excitability to force unconsciousness. Slow-wave synaptic pruning and metabolic restoration. Risk: chronic somnolence and cognitive control failure. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: respects absolute metabolic boundaries against continuous productivity narratives.  
* **Boredom / Low Yield:** Low-amplitude phasic dopamine 18, low reward prediction error tracking, moderate tonic norepinephrine. Downregulates task-relevant precision to force policy abandonment.19 Terminating low-yield exploitation to prompt patch switching. Risk: chronic restlessness and erratic policy switching. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: contextualizes boredom as an adaptive foraging mechanism.  
* **Compulsive Checking:** Hyper-precise prior expectations 19, impaired endocannabinoid termination, direct-pathway dopamine.5 Repeats automated motor routines to resolve unyielding internal uncertainty.19 Securing boundary matrices under extreme predator saturation. Risk: clinical obsessive-compulsive checking traps; routine fixation.19 *High confidence*. Ethical caution: links repetitive behavioral phenotypes to formal statistical tracking errors.  
* **Reward Blunting:** Chronic cytokine-mediated DAT velocity 13, chronic GR desensitization 7, dopamine down-regulation.25 Prevents scaling of incentive salience across all external targets.15 Surviving chronic, non-resolving environmental hostility or confinement. Risk: functional anhedonia and treatment resistance. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: isolates biological debt from psychological character defects.  
* **Effort Avoidance:** Flattening of mesolimbic Expected Value of Control curve 5, central leptin/insulin resistance 12, chronic neuroinflammation.14 Inflates computed weight of behavioral energy costs relative to returns.5 Protecting compromised energy reserves under biological debt or starvation. Risk: permanent operational stagnation. *High confidence*. Ethical caution: shifts clinical focus from motivation failure to underlying bioenergetic insolvency.

### **Artifact H: Endocrine-Brain Loop Map**

| Somatic Axis Origin | Chemical Vector | Physical Entry Route centrally | Target Brain Hubs | Primary Policy Topology Shift | Operational Timescale | Evidence Strength | Clinical Boundary |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Adrenal Axis** | Cortisol.8 | Passive vascular diffusion across barrier lines.7 | Hippocampus, Amygdala, Prefrontal Cortex.7 | Restructures metabolic ledger; optimizes glucose access for defense.8 | Minutes (acute surge) to months (chronic MALT).8 | **High evidence strength** | Tracks the tipping point where adaptive mobilization degrades into mitochondrial failure.7 |
| **Gastric Axis** | Ghrelin.22 | Central transporter crossing and vagal afferent lines.12 | Ventral Tegmental Area, Arcuate Nucleus.12 | Accelerates dopaminergic velocity via GHSR; elevates progressive ratio breakthroughs.12 | Minutes to hours (preprandial spikes).22 | **High evidence strength** | Bounded by overlapping macronutrient availability profiles and peripheral glucose constraints.22 |
| **Adipose Axis** | Leptin.23 | Saturable transporter-mediated crossing arrays.12 | Ventral Tegmental Area, Hypothalamic Hubs.12 | Suppresses motivation to work; dose-dependently lowers breakpoints.12 | Days to weeks (tracking absolute lipid mass reserves).24 | **High evidence strength** | Central leptin resistance disables feedback, mimicking state of starvation.12 |
| **Pancreatic Axis** | Insulin.23 | Receptor-mediated transcytosis mechanisms. | Striatum, Hypothalamus, Hippocampus.12 | Enhances striatal DAT activity; downregulates appetitive cue salience.13 | Hours (coordinated postprandial energy stabilization). | **High evidence strength** | Central insulin resistance uncouples metabolic tracking from cognitive policy execution. |
| **Immune Axis** | Cytokines (IL-6, IL-1beta).14 | Endothelial claudin-5 loss and leaky circumventricular points.26 | Basal Ganglia, Ventral Striatum, Medial PFC.14 | Enforces sickness behavior; downregulates dopamine to shunt energy.15 | Days (acute challenge) to months (chronic neuroinflammation).14 | **High evidence strength** | Distinguishes necessary acute host defense from chronic, destructive neuroinflammatory loads.14 |
| **Gonadal Axis** | Testosterone / Estrogens. | Passive structural steroid crossover paths. | Amygdala, Hypothalamus, Nucleus Accumbens Shell. | Modifies calculated valuation of dominance and status defense.44 | Weeks (hormonal cycles) to lifespan windows (puberty). | **Moderate evidence strength** | Strictly bounded by non-essentialist constraints; outcomes depend entirely on cultural layout. |
| **Thyroid Axis** | T3 / T4 Hormones. | Specialized iodothyronine transporter systems.31 | Comprehensive expression across all central layers.31 | Establishes baseline basal metabolic velocity and transcript rates.31 | Weeks to months (setting macro-scalar operational limits). | **High evidence strength** | Clinical boundaries defined by systemic hypothyroid lethargy or hyperthyroid noise amplification. |

### **Artifact I: Pop-Neuro Myth Correction Table**

| Popular Culture Myth Tropes | Core Neurobiological Error | Systems-Neurobiology Architecture | Canon-Safe Replacement Wording Formulation | Evidence Caveat |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Dopamine = Pleasure Juice** | Confounds reward *wanting* (incentive salience) with reward *liking* (hedonic consumption).28 | Dopamine codes reward prediction errors (delta_n) and opportunity costs (R) to regulate vigor.4 | *Dopamine modulates policy vigor, reward learning, and effort valuation under pathway-specific conditions.* | Human functional neuroimaging lacks the spatial resolution to isolate sub-synaptic cleft dynamics. |
| **Dopamine Detox** | Presumes central neurotransmitter pools can be mechanically drained or reset by brief behavioral fasting. | Receptor density, transporter velocity, and clearance kinetics are non-linear homeostatic feedback loops. | *Tonic-phasic dopaminergic calibration updates the Expected Value of Control relative to baseline opportunity costs.* | Population-level behavioral correlations do not map onto the real-time receptor density of an individual. |
| **Serotonin = Happiness Fluid** | Reduces a complex multi-pathway coping matrix into a simple scalar marker of psychological mood.39 | Serotonin coordinates responses to adversity, balancing passive moderation (5-HT1A) vs. plasticity (5-HT2A).39 | *Serotonin participates in behavioral inhibition, temporal horizon, aversive regulation, and affective flexibility through receptor-specific pathways.* | Chronic reuptake blockade induces sweeping downstream adaptations crossing multiple network boundaries.43 |
| **Oxytocin = Love Hormone** | Omits oxytocin’s context-dependent intensification of in-group favoritism and aggressive out-group xenophobia. | Oxytocin functions as a social salience tuner, boosting interpersonal cue precision relative to structural priors.28 | *Oxytocin increases the salience of social information, which can support bonding or defensive in-group dynamics depending on context.* | Central volume transmission dynamics dissociate completely from peripheral blood plasma assays. |
| **Cortisol = Bad Stress Chemical** | Converts an essential, highly adaptive allostatic mobilization signal into an inherently toxic biological poison.8 | Cortisol restructures the body's glucose economy to ensure central systems can fund high-urgency actions.8 | *Cortisol mobilizes resources under anticipated demand; chronic dysregulation shifts the cost structure and damages recovery capacity.* | Systemic vascular measurements do not reconstruct localized prefrontal receptor resistance patterns.8 |
| **Endorphins = Runner’s High Only** | Attributes complex post-exertion recovery to a single peptide class, omitting retrograde endocannabinoid dynamics.48 | Endogenous opioids act selectively within limbic hotspots to validate consumptive success and signal relief.28 | *Endogenous opioids gate hedonic consumption validation and signal systemic relief to initiate metabolic recovery policies.* | Central opioid receptor binding profiles operate independently of circulating peripheral blood metrics.20 |
| **Ghrelin = Simple Hunger Switch** | Treats a complex modifier of mesolimbic cost curves as a simple mechanical trigger for eating behavior.12 | Ghrelin acts directly within the VTA via GHSR to accelerate dopaminergic velocity and elevate breakpoints.12 | *These metabolic hormones modify the mesolimbic effort-discounting curve, shifting the progressive ratio breakpoint for reward pursuit.* | Receptor sensitivity curves can decouple from absolute peripheral concentration parameters under strain.24 |
| **Leptin = Simple Fullness Switch** | Omits leptin's direct down-regulation of reward-directed progressive ratio work investment within the VTA.12 | Leptin tracks systemic wealth to suppress motivation to work by binding directly to VTA LepR grids.12 | *Leptin signaling acts centrally to modify the computed cost structure of effort investment, downregulating reward wanting.* | Chronic metabolic overload drives central leptin resistance, masking available bioenergetic reserves.12 |
| **GLP-1 = Willpower in a Syringe** | Mischaracterizes top-down moralized cognitive control as a simple peripheral gastric peptide injection.13 | GLP-1R engagement increases striatal surface DAT expression, accelerating dopamine clearance to lower cue salience.13 | *GLP-1 signaling can alter satiety, food cue salience, reward valuation, and metabolic policy control under specific clinical and physiological conditions.* | Commercial long-acting variants utilize structural adjustments that bypass native regulatory parameters.22 |
| **Cytokines = Depression Trigger** | Simplifies an active, highly evolved immunometabolic resource preservation shunt into a psychological defect.15 | Cytokines downregulate striatal dopamine synthesis and enhance clearance to fund baseline host defense.14 | *Cytokine signaling retunes motivation toward conservation, withdrawal, healing, pain sensitivity, and threat containment during immune demand.* | Blood serum cytokine arrays display extreme individual variability and lack direct central mapping precision. |
| **Testosterone = Pure Violence** | Establishes a primitive causal link, ignoring that testosterone reinforces status-preservation and dominant policies. | Testosterone increases computed value of status maintenance, manifesting as cooperation or competition based on rules. | *Testosterone modulates the computed valuation of status-preservation and dominance policies within prevailing social constraints.* | Statistical population-level correlations do not dictate the real-time policy choice of an individual agent. |
| **Chemical Imbalance Narrative** | Presents complex psychiatric states as a simple volumetric shortage or surplus of a single fluid class within a brain tank.40 | Psychiatric phenotypes reflect the active inference engine adjusting operational settings under bioenergetic constraints.8 | *Psychiatric phenotypes reflect the active inference engine adjusting operational parameters to navigate compromised bioenergetic constraints or severe environmental volatility.* | Post-mortem neurochemical assays cannot reconstruct the live, informational routing of functional networks. |
| **Hormones Made Me Do It** | Assumes peripheral endocrine signaling overrides all cognitive architecture to force unmediated behaviors. | Endocrine hormones modify baseline policy cost parameters and affordability matrices without breaking inference loops. | *Hormonal vectors adjust the prior probability coordinates and resource boundaries of the generative model under constraint.* | Individual developmental trajectory and active environmental interfaces alter receptor density grids. |
| **Reward System Rewired** | Presumes a permanent, destructive hardware alteration that destroys all future cognitive agency and choice. | Corticostriatal loops adjust their baseline synaptic weights dynamically relative to prediction errors and state variables.5 | *Chronic high-amplitude prediction errors shift the baseline synaptic weighting of corticostriatal loops, biasing the system toward short-horizon policies.* | Microstructural plastic changes remain continuously moderated by global volume transmission grids.16 |
| **Adrenal Fatigue Diagnostics** | Postulates a mechanical collapse of adrenal cortisol production capacities that is clinically non-existent. | Chronic hypercortisolemia drives central glucocorticoid receptor resistance and Mitochondrial Allostatic Load (MALT).7 | *Chronic allostatic load induces glucocorticoid receptor desensitization and drives subcellular mitochondrial dynamic failure.* | Localized prefrontal receptor resistance can occur without changing raw circulating serum cortisol levels.8 |
| **Neurotransmitter Typing Profiles** | Uses internet personality typologies to link complex human characters to a single dominant monoamine asset. | Human behavior emerges from non-linear interactions across an integrated, multi-layered chemical mixing board layout. | *Individual behavioral phenotypes express the dynamic equilibrium of an integrated, multi-scalar chemical tuning board.* | Static personality categorizations ignore the radical context-dependency and environmental embedding of active inference. |

| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Blood Dopamine Measures** | Assumed to reflect central mesolimbic or nigrostriatal motivational velocity. | Assessing peripheral autonomic stress boundaries or tracking pheochromocytoma phenotypes. | Diagnosing central neurodivergence profiles or predicting individual task completion vigor. | Must combine with central high-resolution PET ligands and structured operant tasks. |
| **PET Receptor Binding** | Interpreted as a real-time map of synaptic neurotransmitter exocytosis kinetics. | Quantifying long-term changes in absolute structural receptor density limits across cohorts.43 | Treating static tracer displacement readouts as a direct translation of subjective affect. | Requires synchronization with localized microdialysis baselines and simultaneous fMRI matrices. |
| **CSF Metabolite Assays** | Assumed to reflect localized neurotransmitter turnover velocities within discrete circuits. | Tracking macro-scalar enzymatic adjustments and monitoring gross pharmacological compliance. | Using lumbar puncture metrics to explain individual moral choices or specific emotional states. | Must calibrate against direct electrophysiological unit recordings in validated animal models.38 |
| **Salivary Cortisol Sampling** | Interpreted as a direct readout of the absolute allostatic load of the central nervous system.8 | Documenting macro-scalar circadian rhythm integrity and indexing the awakening response.8 | Utilizing single-point samples to justify supplement selection or diagnose systemic "burnout." | Demands complete multi-point diurnal slope tracking paired with dexamethasone suppression tests.8 |
| **Diurnal Cortisol Slope** | Assumed to plot the precise rate of systemic neuroendocrine structural decompensation.8 | Characterizing long-term hyper- or hypocortisolemic states in heavily stressed cohorts.8 | Inferring an individual's immediate cognitive control capacity from a single week's curve profiles. | Must align with high-resolution sleep architecture metrics and metabolic energy ledgers. |

| **Serum Ghrelin Assays** | Assumed to reflect the precise magnitude of central appetitive novelty-seeking drive.12 | Investigating macro-scalar metabolic rhythm disruptions and documenting gastric clearing rates.22 | Explaining individual impulsive eating behaviors entirely via vascular peptide fluctuations. | Must cross-check against central fMRI food-cue salience tasks and overnight fasting records.12 |
| **Vascular GLP-1 Tracking** | Assumed to plot the direct operational velocity of central preproglucagon satiety gates.12 | Monitoring baseline metabolic incretin responses following standardized macronutrient entry.22 | Mapping individual psychological willpower limits based on peripheral peptide curves.13 | Central effects must triangulate with structural insula and orbitofrontal fMRI metrics.13 |
| **Testosterone Assays** | Assumed to serve as a linear, unmediated readout of an individual's physical aggression drive. | Diagnosing clinical hypogonadism and tracking macro-scalar endocrine development windows. | Explaining specific instances of violent behavior as a mechanical consequence of high serum levels. | Must calibrate against explicit socio-cultural rules, status grids, and behavioral tasks. |
| **Estrogen Assays** | Assumed to dictate real-time emotional variance and lock agents into fixed reactive phenotypes. | Monitoring follicular phase transitions and tracking lifespan developmental menopausal states. | Assigning complex cognitive policy shifts entirely to vascular steroid concentration dips. | Requires matching with comprehensive lifestyle records, sleep metrics, and active inference tasks. |
| **HRV Measurement Profiles** | Assumed to plot the absolute real-time tone of the central autonomic predictive engine. | Documenting macro-scalar physical training adaptations and tracking recovery timelines. | Using consumer smartwatch metrics to claim an individual lacks top-down regulatory control. | Must align with precise respiratory sinus arrhythmia tracking and lab-grade ECG records. |
| **Pupillometry Metrics** | Assumed to carry a direct, noise-free code of locus coeruleus noradrenergic spikes.31 | Indexing changes in baseline arousal states and mapping surprise parameters during tasks.31 | Interpreting brief pupil fluctuations as direct proof of psychological deception or hidden intent. | Demands strict control normalization against ambient light entry and micro-saccade tracks.19 |
| **Pharmacological Challenges** | Assumed to reveal the baseline chemical deficit status of an individual's central networks.43 | Characterizing receptor-specific drug mechanisms and mapping system response variance across cohorts. | Inferring that because a ligand alters a phenotype, a pre-existing volumetric deficit caused it.41 | Must evaluate downstream changes across multiple interconnected neurotransmitter systems.16 |
| **Self-Report Mood Scales** | Assumed to carry an objective, linear readout of central monoaminergic parameter states.41 | Mapping phenomenological distress trends and tracking clinical symptom variance over time. | Treating a subject's descriptive linguistic checkmarks as absolute proof of a chemical deficit.41 | Must cross-check against objective operant task velocities and capability metrics.15 |
| **Digital Reward Metrics** | Assumed to measure the precise volumetric depletion of an individual's central dopamine tanks. | Tracking micro-scalar platform interaction loops and mapping interface behavioral capture velocity. | Claiming that internet application usage physically "rewires" the basic hardware of the brain. | Requires matching with formal computational reinforcement learning models and fMRI focus grids.17 |

## **21. Evidence Ledger**

The ledger below maps the core empirical foundations of the chemical tuning-board model, using the evidence tier definitions from Report B to prevent individual diagnosis or moralized biological assertions.

| Claim Statement | Claim Type | Evidence Type | Level(s) of Analysis | Confidence Label | Scope Conditions | Interpretive Caveat | Representative Sources | What Would Change Confidence |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **LC-NE triggers astrocytic glycogenolysis via beta2-AR to export lactate.** | Mechanism | Mechanistic Evidence / Computational Model.1 | Cellular NVU to Network Drive.1 | **High confidence** | Dependent on localized cAMP second messenger transduction cascades.1 | Astrocyte-to-neuron shuttle velocity must match real-time neuronal consumption rates.1 | Hertz et al., Zorec et al., NGV Model.1 | In vivo visualization of real-time cell-specific lactate transport under optogenetic challenge. |
| **High-frequency LC activation reduces regional cerebral blood flow.** | Observed Fact | Experimental Finding / Animal Model.33 | Microvascular to Regional Parenchyma.33 | **Moderate confidence** | Dependent on specific electrical stimulation frequencies (15-20 Hz).33 | Vasoconstrictive pericyte tension varies across distinct sensory cortical layers.33 | Goadsby, Katayama, de la Torre.33 | Direct high-resolution imaging of capillary diameter adjustments in alert, behaving primates. |
| **Tonic striatal dopamine reports the ecological average reward rate (R).** | Formal Model | Computational Synthesis / Association.4 | Striatal Volume Matrix to Behavioral Velocity.29 | **High confidence** | Validated within free-operant instrumental schedules tracking response latency.29 | Cannot model sudden structural shifts that alter state space coordinates.32 | Niv, Daw, Dayan, Westbrook & Cools.4 | Failure of temporal difference vigor predictions in naturalistic foraging paradigms. |
| **Prefrontal D1 receptors stabilize goals while D2 permits updating.** | Mechanism | Theoretical Synthesis / In Vitro Recording.6 | Prefrontal Recurrent Microcircuits.6 | **High confidence** | Regulated by biphasic dopamine concentration thresholds.5 | Extensive receptor co-localization on single dendrites creates non-linear signaling.5 | Cools, Seamans & Yang, Fallon et al..5 | Real-time observation of Layer V pyramid state transitions in awake primates during task switches. |
| **Chronic high-dose glucocorticoids drive mitochondrial fragmentation.** | Subcellular Mechanism | Clinical Finding / In Vitro Assay.7 | Mitochondrial Quality Control to Limbic Atrophy.7 | **High confidence** | Bounded by the depletion of anti-apoptotic mitochondrial Bcl-2 complexes.7 | Acute low-dose exposure reverses this effect, enhancing neuroprotection.7 | Du, McEwen, Manji, Picard Lab, Lapp et al. | Disproof of GR-mediated nuclear translocation pathways inside alert cortical neurons. |
| **APOE4 genetic variants exhibit heightened hippocampal GR activation.** | Observed Fact | Transgenic Animal Model / RNA-Seq.54 | Genomic Profile to Hippocampal Pathology.54 | **Moderate confidence** | Validated in middle-aged rodent backgrounds tracking tau hyperphosphorylation.54 | Direct translation to human clinical Alzheimer's progression timelines remains unresolved. | BioRxiv 2025, Alzheimer's Risk Consortium.54 | Longitudinal human imaging tracking real-time GR binding velocity across APOE carriers. |
| **Trusted social proximity decreases the perceived cost of the environment.** | Ecological Observation | Psychophysical fMRI Proxy / Perception Assay.9 | Social Network Network Proximity to Individual Sensory Layers.9 | **Moderate confidence** | Regulated by subjective parameters of baseline familiarity and relationship trust.9 | Perceived negative or adversarial social resources reverse the effect, increasing load.11 | Coan, Proffitt, Schnall, Zadra et al..9 | Direct demonstration that social buffering fails when accounting for absolute metabolic assets. |
| **Ghrelin binds VTA GHSR to invigorate progressive ratio breakpoints.** | Mechanism | Animal Model / Micro-injection Challenge.12 | Gastric Peptide Vector to Mesolimbic Dopamine Firing.12 | **High confidence** | Requires intact D1/D2 signaling lines inside the nucleus accumbens shell.12 | High-yield localized exocytosis can override baseline postprandial satiety gates.12 | PMC 10330780, Central Feeding Review.12 | Disproof of direct VTA->NAc dopaminergic acceleration during physiological fasting. |
| **Leptin binds VTA receptors to downregulate progressive ratio breakpoints.** | Mechanism | Animal Model / Chemogenetic Tracking.12 | Adipokine Vector to PR Breakpoint Valuation.12 | **High confidence** | Selectively discounts high-effort physical investments without changing baseline consumption.12 | Central leptin resistance decouples peripheral mass from central motivation loops.12 | LepR Tracking Consortium, Farooqi et al..12 | Clinical trial showing exogenous leptin changes effort metrics in resistant human cohorts. |
| **GLP-1 increases striatal DAT expression to accelerate dopamine clearance.** | Mechanism | Mechanistic Evidence / Radioligand Assay.13 | Hindbrain PPG Axons to Striatal Synaptic Cleft.13 | **High confidence** | Confirmed via direct pharmacological tracer clearance protocols in rodent models.13 | Therapeutic analog velocity configurations may exceed native physiological boundaries.12 | Jensen et al., Hernandez & Schmidt.13 | Human PET data showing immediate DAT binding updates after acute GLP-1R challenge. |
| **GLP-1 receptor activation upregulates central anti-apoptotic Bcl-2.** | Downstream Mechanism | In Vitro Assay / Western Blot.13 | Central GPCR Cascades to Microglial Excitotoxicity.13 | **Moderate confidence** | Driven by cAMP/PKA/CREB signaling sequences inside target neurons.13 | Most data stems from neuroprotective trauma models rather than baseline tracking. | Erbil et al., Graham et al..13 | Demonstration that native, non-pharmacological central GLP-1 lacks anti-inflammatory reach. |
| **Dorsal raphe serotonergic firing rates elevate during active waiting.** | Observed Fact | Single-Unit Electrophysiology.38 | Raphe Pacemaker Cells to Forebrain Restraint Gates.38 | **High confidence** | Firing collapses instantly if the delay interval exceeds calculated reward return probabilities.38 | Phasic bursts during aversive encounters operate on separate mathematical lines.18 | Airy et al., DRN Unit Recording Group.38 | Optogenetic silencing of tonic DRN neurons that preserves waiting patience parameters. |
| **Serotonin branches into 5-HT1A stress buffering and 5-HT2A plasticity.** | Theoretical Synthesis | Computational Pharmacology / Clinical Tracking.39 | 5-HT1A-5-HT2A Structural Balance to Coping Policies.39 | **High confidence** | Explains complementary mechanics of conventional SSRIs and classic psychedelic agonists.39 | Ignores intermediate contributions from remaining receptor subtypes (5-HT4-5-HT7).39 | Carhart-Harris & Nutt, Synthesis Matrix.39 | Discovery of a single ligand that simultaneously engages both paths to produce matching states. |
| **Orexin projections to the LC stabilize sleep-to-wake transitions.** | Observed Fact | Optogenetic Challenge / Local Micro-injection.21 | Lateral Hypothalamus to Stem Noradrenergic Nodes.21 | **High confidence** | Frequency-dependent (>5 Hz); critical for setting global arousal thresholds.21 | Knockout models maintain matching net sleep amounts but express fragmentation.21 | Adamantidis, de Lecea, Sakurai, Mochizuki.21 | Isolation of an adjacent non-orexinergic population that fully restores transition stability. |
| **Histaminergic TMN neurons discharge tonically during waking phases.** | Observed Fact | Single-Cell RT-PCR / Unit Recording.55 | Tuberomammillary Nucleus to Neocortex Grid.55 | **High confidence** | Coordinates qualitative cognitive attention while orexin directs locomotion execution.56 | Firing drops to absolute silence during both slow-wave and REM sleep phases.55 | Anaclet et al., Parmentier et al., Siegel.56 | Demonstration that histamine loss preserves baseline cortical EEG spectral power distributions. |
| **Peripheral cytokines blunted ventral striatal reward anticipation responses.** | Observed Fact | Human Functional Neuroimaging / Interferon Models.14 | Circulating Cytokines to Basal Ganglia Motivation Loops.14 | **High confidence** | Human verification based on longitudinal clinical cancer medication tracking models.14 | Reversing peripheral inflammation does not immediately restore central dopamine turnover curves.14 | Felger, Miller, Harrison, Eisenberger, Emory Group.14 | Failure to replicate striatal reward blunting in wide-scale autoimmune clinical trials. |
| **Peripheral interferon surges activate endothelial PGE2 to cause aversion.** | Mechanism | Animal Model / Conditioned Place Aversion Assay.27 | Brain Endothelial Crossing to Nigrostriatal Nodes.27 | **Moderate confidence** | Dependent on specific endothelial cell activation via MyD88 signaling sequences.27 | Structural blocking of PGE2 synthesis may provoke alternative inflammatory load lines.27 | Striatal D2-KO Consortium, Trends in Cognitive Sciences.15 | Human confirmation that blocking endothelial prostaglandin blocks cytokine-induced dysphoria. |

## **22. Annotated Bibliography**

* **Carhart-Harris, R. L., & Nutt, D. J. (2017). Serotonin and brain function: a tale of two receptors. *Psychopharmacology*, 234(9), 1623–1639.** 39  
  * *Significance:* Formulates the bipartite model of central serotonergic function, demonstrating that serotonin enhances two distinct, opposing adaptive strategies to environmental adversity. Postsynaptic 5-HT1A receptor activation mediates passive coping and baseline stress moderation by hyperpolarizing limbic structures. Conversely, Layer V cortical pyramidal 5-HT2A engagement drives active coping, structural neural remodeling, and psychological flexibility, explaining the divergent clinical parameters of conventional reuptake inhibitors vs. classic psychedelic agonists.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Models focus predominantly on high-density cortical and limbic expressions; downstream interactions with minor serotonergic receptor arrays (5-HT4, 5-HT6, 5-HT7) are excluded from the core mathematical formulation.  
* **Niv, Y., Daw, N. D., Joel, D., & Dayan, P. (2007). Tonic dopamine: opportunity costs and the control of response vigor. *Psychopharmacology*, 191(3), 507–520.** 4  
  * *Significance:* Establishes the formal mathematical reinforcement learning architecture that treats ambient, tonic striatal dopamine concentrations as a computational proxy for the long-run average reward rate (R) within a local ecology. Within free-operant behavioral environments, this signal acts as the opportunity cost of time, meaning that high tonic dopamine mathematically penalizes behavioral inactivity, thereby shifting response latencies to invigorate motor and cognitive vigor.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Validated across free-operant instrumental schedules tracking latency metrics; cannot predict policy re-indexing parameters during unexpected structural transformations of the state space matrix.  
* **Cools, R. (2015). The cost of dopamine for dynamic cognitive control. *Current Opinion in Behavioral Sciences*, 4, 152–159.** 6  
  * *Significance:* Reconceptualizes top-down cognitive control as an active cost-benefit decision framework regulated by striatal-prefrontal dopaminergic balance rather than an unmediated implementation capacity. Demonstrates that prefrontal D1 receptor pathways elevate local energy barriers to robustly stabilize current goal representations, while mesocortical D2 pathways lower barriers to permit flexible model updating, establishing a non-linear baseline where individual drug responses depend on baseline neurochemical assets.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Human findings rely on acute oral pharmacological challenges in healthy volunteer cohorts; cannot directly map the chronic microstructural adaptations seen in clinical neurodegenerative phenotypes.  
* **Picard, M., & McEwen, B. S. (2014). Mitochondrial allostatic load puts the 'gluc' back in glucocorticoids. *Nature Reviews Endocrinology*, 10(5), 303–310.** 8  
  * *Significance:* Constructs the subcellular framework of Mitochondrial Allostatic Load (MALT), detailing the biological continuum through which acute, adaptive glucocorticoid resource mobilization transitions into chronic structural decompensation under non-resolving stress. Maps the exact tipping point where glucocorticoid receptor down-regulation and anti-apoptotic depletion prompt irreversible mitochondrial fragmentation, uncontrolled oxidative stress, and the release of sterile inflammatory DAMPs.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Synthesizes macro-scalar systemic endocrine tracking with central structural neurobiology; does not isolate the exact chronological boundaries required for microstructural tissue recovery loops.  
* **Coan, J. A., & Sbarra, D. A. (2015). Social Baseline Theory: The social regulation of risk and effort. *Current Opinion in Psychology*, 1, 87–91.** 9  
  * *Significance:* Formalizes Social Baseline Theory within a bioenergetic and active inference framework, proving that the human brain evolved to treat close proximity to reliable social partners as its primary ecological default state. Demonstrates that social scaffolding maps directly as a formal energetic asset interchangeable with metabolic resources, allowing individuals to outsource threat vigilance and load-sharing costs to systematically flatten the environmental cost profile.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Bounded strictly by subjective parameters of baseline relationship familiarity and trust; uncalibrated, chaotic, or hostile social proximity reverses the asset valuation into a steep active resource cost.  
* **Felger, J. C., & Miller, A. H. (2012). Cytokines, dopamine and activation of the basal ganglia: implications for fatigue and anhedonia. *Brain, Behavior, and Immunity*, 26(8), 1199–1209.** 14  
  * *Significance:* Outlines the precise neuroinflammatory pathways through which peripheral immune cytokines target the monoaminergic architecture of the basal ganglia to enforce behavioral conservation. Documents that chronic cytokine exposure activates local microglia, upregulates presynaptic surface DAT velocity, and disrupts dopamine synthesis, steepening the effort-discounting curve to produce clinical anhedonia, fatigue, and psychomotor slowing.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* High-density evidence is derived from human longitudinal clinical tracking models utilizing therapeutic Interferon-alpha interventions; chronic low-grade sterile inflammation profiles require distinct validation tracks.  
* **de Lecea, L., & Adamantidis, A. (2014). Orexins/hypocretins: critical regulators of arousal stability. *Frontiers in Behavioral Neuroscience*, 8, 16.** 21  
  * *Significance:* Integrates the structural actions of lateral hypothalamic orexinergic neuropeptides, proving they function as primary stabilizers of the brain's behavioral state architecture rather than simple appetite switches. Shows that frequency-dependent orexin release depolarizes locus coeruleus stem noradrenergic nodes, raising global arousal thresholds to prevent disorganized sleep-wake transitions and ensure policy continuity during tasks.  
  * *Scope Conditions & Limitations:* Relies heavily on high-precision optogenetic and chemogenetic rodent challenges; human clinical validation remains bounded by post-hoc tracking of narcoleptic and cataplectic cohorts.57

## **23. Canon Handoff Summary**

### **Ten Core Preservation Principles**

1. **Chemical Control Parameters:** Reject single-molecule "mood chemical" folklores; treat chemical arrays as context-sensitive parameters adjusting precision, vigor, and learning rates.17  
2. **Tonic Dopamine as Time Cost:** Maintain the computational formulation where tonic striatal dopamine reports the long-run average reward rate (R), functioning as the opportunity cost of sloth.4  
3. **Biphasic Noradrenergic Gain:** Preserve the dual operational states of the locus coeruleus: task-locked phasic focus vs. high-volatility tonic network reset driving environmental exploration.29  
4. **ACh Sensory Precision Tuning:** Route acetylcholine as the formal manager of expected uncertainty, amplifying bottom-up prediction error precision while dampening horizontal priors.19  
5. **Bipartite Serotonergic Coping:** Map serotonin through its structural receptor bifurcation: 5-HT1A hyperpolarizing stress moderation vs. 5-HT2A structural cognitive plasticity.39  
6. **Liking vs. Wanting Disconnection:** Isolate mesolimbic dopaminergic wanting (incentive salience) from endogenous opioid mu-receptor hedonic hotspot liking validation.28  
7. **Social Scaffolding Asset Value:** Integrate Social Baseline Theory, treating proximity to trusted social resources directly as a formal bioenergetic asset that flattens environmental cost profiles.9  
8. **Mitochondrial Allostatic Load (MALT):** Track the tipping point where chronic hypercortisolemia transitions from adaptive resource mobilization to irreversible mitochondrial fragmentation.7  
9. **Metabolic Effort Valuation:** Route peripheral signals (GLP-1, leptin, ghrelin) directly into midbrain nodes to dynamically rewrite the computed Expected Value of Control.12  
10. **Immune-Motivational Retuning:** Institutionalize sickness behavior as an active resource preservation policy that downregulates striatal dopamine to fund systemic physiological defense.15

### **Ten Overclaim Patterns to Avoid**

1. **The Pleasure-Juice Trope:** Do not write that dopamine release directly manufactures sensory pleasure or hedonic satisfaction.28  
2. **The Dopamine Detox Illusion:** Avoid claiming that human receptor sensitivities can be mechanically reset through brief behavioral fasting.  
3. **The Serotonin-Deficit Myth:** Reject the narrative that clinical major depression represents a direct volumetric shortage of serotonin fluid in a static brain tank.40  
4. **The Love Hormone Generalization:** Never formulate oxytocin as a universal guarantee of unconditional empathy or non-exclusive prosocial trust.28  
5. **The Cortisol as Poison Fallacy:** Do not define cortisol as an inherently toxic element, omitting its essential role in circadian energy distribution and resource access.8  
6. **The Aggression Hormone Essentialism:** Avoid stating that testosterone drives unmediated physical violence, ignoring its modulation of context-dependent status defense.  
7. **The Willpower in a Syringe Metaphor:** Reject claims that GLP-1 agonists inject top-down cognitive willpower, omitting their acceleration of striatal dopamine clearance.13  
8. **The Adrenal Fatigue Diagnostic Folklore:** Never adopt the invalid non-clinical claim of exhausted cortisol synthesis pools, replacing it with central GR desensitization models.8  
9. **The Correlation to Phenotype Leap:** Avoid transforming population-level neurochemical association metrics into deterministic individual behavioral diagnoses.  
10. **The Model-to-Prescription Conversion:** Do not convert descriptive systems-neurobiology maps into immediate clinical or nutritional supplement intervention prescriptions.

### **Core Structural Vocabulary Conventions**

* *Instead of "dopamine causes motivation," use:* **"Dopamine modulates policy vigor, reward learning, and effort valuation under pathway-specific conditions."** 4  
* *Instead of "serotonin is happiness," use:* **"Serotonin participates in behavioral inhibition, temporal horizon, aversive regulation, and affective flexibility through receptor-specific pathways."** 38  
* *Instead of "oxytocin creates love," use:* **"Oxytocin increases the salience of social information, which can support bonding or defensive in-group dynamics depending on context."** 9  
* *Instead of "cortisol is bad stress," use:* **"Cortisol mobilizes resources under anticipated demand; chronic dysregulation shifts the cost structure and damages recovery capacity."** 8  
* *Instead of "GLP-1 gives willpower," use:* **"GLP-1 signaling can alter satiety, food cue salience, reward valuation, and metabolic policy control under specific clinical and physiological conditions."** 12

### **Canonical Analytical Sequence Template**

Every future volume analysis tracking neurochemical state shifts must pass sequentially through the technical routing chain:

Somatic / Ecological Signal Source -> Receptor Subtype / Anatomical Target Routing -> Computational Matrix Parameter Shift -> Behavioral Policy Selection Bias -> Long-Term Allostatic / Metabolic Consequence

### **Unresolved Inquiries for Report F**

1. Through what specific neuroimmune signaling pathways does the transition from acute sickness conservation to chronic low-grade neuroinflammation permanently disrupt the slow-wave sleep delta power architecture required for glymphatic structural clearance?  
2. What are the precise computational and receptor-specific boundaries where long-acting central GLP-1R saturation shifts from adaptive reward cue-dampening to pathological, wide-scale anhedonia across non-food incentive landscapes?  
3. By what precise molecular feedback mechanism does the localized loss of astrocytic glycogen reserves under chronic, high-frequency noradrenergic volume transmission accelerate tau phosphorylation and hypervascular leakage within the locus coeruleus core?  
4. How does the central active inference engine mathematically represent the bioenergetic value of digital and technologically entangled social scaffolding before selecting an outsourcing policy vs. a policy of self-reliant threat hypervigilance?  
5. What are the exact receptor-region cross-talk pathways that govern the deceleration and successful termination of the hypothalamic-pituitary-adrenal axis when retrograde endocannabinoid transients engage amygdalar presynaptic CB1 receptors during fear extinction learning?
